Shanghai-Xiamen Radio Out of Service

▲ Due to Damage to Radio Station Equipment

▲ Will be Able to Send and Receive Normally Today

The shortwave radio station of the Ministry of Communications from Shanghai to Xiamen suddenly reported damage to its equipment yesterday morning and was unable to send and receive. The station sent workers to repair it, and it was not until after 3:00 PM that it returned to its original state. Therefore, wireless telegrams from Shanghai to Xiamen yesterday morning were all returned.

Donggang Ship Out of Danger

The Donggang ship, owned by Mr. Zhao Yangfu of this port, was rented to the Yadong Company and sailed on the route from Shanghai to Min to Xinghua to Quanzhou. On the 20th of this month, when sailing to the Shuangfeng waters of the Min Sea, the steam pipe burst, and the ship's hold flooded by four feet. Forty passengers were rescued to Fuzhou by the Sanbei Wanxiang ship, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, this port received a telegram from Fuzhou saying that the Donggang ship had been towed to Dongchong in Fuzhou by the Jixiang warship and has now docked at the pier. All crew members are safe. Many of the goods in the ship's cabins were damaged by water stains, and it is necessary to investigate the details before it can be known. The ship has decided to stay in Fuzhou for repairs before sailing to Shanghai again. As for the cause of the accident and the extent of the damage, the ship owner has not yet reported.

Renji Hospital Medical Report

Renji Hospital recently released its 1930 report. The hospital treated a total of 133,121 outpatients and 1,869 inpatients throughout the year. All hospital beds were in constant use, with an occupancy rate of 99%. 1,575 people had X-rays. According to symptom statistics, the hospital treated 2,708 people injured in traffic accidents throughout the year, with 1,936 injured by automobiles alone. In addition, 2,680 people were injured in other accidental events and 1,114 people attempted suicide, including 504 men and 610 women. The total expenditure for the year was 203,287.72 taels, while the total donations received were 23,875.11 taels, including 7,311.57 taels from the Race Club, 8,884.06 taels from Western organizations and individuals, 7,679.48 taels from Chinese organizations and individuals, plus 20,000 taels from the Municipal Council, 3,000 taels from the Public Works Department, more than 30,000 taels in miscellaneous income, and more than 69,000 taels in income from the Dehe Fund. The income and expenditure offset each other, still short by 53,566.69 taels.

Nameless Male Corpse Found in Lujiazui

At 11:00 AM yesterday, the No. 1281 sampan of the Customs Water Police Station found a nameless male corpse in the water off Lujiazui in Pudong. The upper body was wearing a Chinese-style white willow-striped cloth short shirt, and the lower body was wearing yellow Western-style trousers. The corpse was about twenty years old. The corpse has now been collected and coffined by the Nanshi Lifesaving Bureau, awaiting identification.

Another Free Clinic Opens in Zhabei

Among the free clinic organizations in the Baoshan Road area of Zhabei is the Tongren Summer Vacation Free Clinic and Medicine Distribution Association, which is organized by some colleagues from the Commercial Press and funded by donations. It is held every summer vacation, saving countless poor and sick people. This year's clinic has already opened a few days ago, and the medical affairs are still voluntarily presided over by the traditional Chinese medicine doctor Zhang Juying. The association is located in the residence of Mr. Zhang in Baoshan Lane, Baoshan Road. Those who are extremely poor can receive medical treatment without paying a consultation fee and receive free medicine.

Fire at Wansheng Sock Factory

The Wansheng Sock Factory, located at No. 26, Hainan West Lane, South Street, Hai Chao Temple, outside Xiaonanmen, Nanshi, was drying yarn with a furnace in the back drying room because it had been raining for days and all the yarn could not be exposed to sunlight. Unexpectedly, at around 4:00 PM yesterday, while drying, a fire was accidentally left on a yarn package. In an instant, smoke filled the air, and fierce flames soared. By the time they tried to rescue it, it was already beyond salvation. Before long, the fire broke through the roof. When the Firefighting Association heard the news, they immediately rang the bell to warn. Soon, the fire brigades from various districts drove out their pump trucks and came to the scene to connect water and extinguish the fire. After about 20 minutes, the fire was extinguished. In this battle, a one-bay flat-roofed drying room at the back of the factory was burned. Afterwards, Zhang Suhou, the police chief of the first section and third branch in charge, heard the alarm and went to the scene, and brought Li Baochang, the headman of the drying room from Anhui, back to the office. During the preliminary hearing by Section Chief Jin, Li confessed the previous situation. Because it was a fire case, he was ordered to stay temporarily to investigate the cause of the fire before further investigation. It is said that the factory's loss was still slight this time. Fortunately, it was discovered early, otherwise the factory was surrounded by thatched houses, and the residents inside were mostly poor people. If the fire spread to the thatched houses, it would inevitably cause a major disaster.

Post Office Opens Mail Service for Insurance Safe Deposit Boxes to Czechoslovakia

According to Shanghai Post Office news, starting from July 1 this year, the Shanghai Postal Administration began to accept insurance safe deposit boxes to Czechoslovakia, which will be transported by German mail ships via the Suez route. The amount of insurance is limited to 2,500 gold francs.

Famous Calligraphers and Painters Raise Funds for the Guangdong Disaster

Lingnan calligrapher Lin Fengmang, also known as the Master of Xihe, recently, due to the severe disaster in Guangdong, specially invited Zhang Yisheng, a calligraphy and painting expert from Yushan, to jointly organize a calligraphy and painting exhibition to raise funds for the Guangdong disaster. They prepared hundreds of works of various sizes, numbered them, and adopted a lottery method. Each ticket costs five yuan, which can be used to draw a number to collect the item. Calligraphy and inscriptions will be written on the spot. The proceeds from the sale of tickets, after deducting the mounting and inking fees, will all be allocated to the fundraising organization, so that they can be sent to the disaster area. The exhibition and lottery dates are set for August 15th and 16th. The items will be distributed on the 17th. The sale of tickets has already started, and various groups such as the Guangzhao Public Office and the Guangdong Overseas Chinese Federation are selling them on consignment. Both gentlemen are teachers in Guangdong primary and secondary schools, and their works are not easy to obtain. This sacrifice for the disaster victims is especially commendable. The venue is the Guangdong Primary and Secondary School.

Business Administration Association Dinner Discussion

▲ Lecture on the Northeast Problem

Yesterday, the Business Administration Association held its 13th dinner discussion at the Lianhua General Association. Shou Yicheng was elected chairman. It was originally planned to invite Professor He Zuilian from Nankai University in Tianjin to give a lecture, but Mr. He received a telegram from Tianjin urging him to return north immediately. Therefore, Chen Binhe was invited to lecture on the Northeast problem. Dai Zhiqian, who had been engaged in industry in the Eastern Provinces, was then invited to lecture on the economic problems of Dongshan Province, which was extremely detailed. Then, Ji Jiannan reported on the situation of the petition in Beijing. The meeting adjourned at around 2:00 PM.

World Trust Examination Begins Presale

Cheng Lianjun, General Manager of Shanghai Trust Co., Ltd., based on his more than 20 years of trust experience in the United States, has compiled and written a book. The content is rich in collection and detailed in records. It uses the history of trust as a wedge to promote a new "Sinicized" trust enterprise. The whole book is divided into 18 chapters, totaling 300,000 words, and bound into a large volume. It is the only specialized book on modern Chinese trust studies. Chapters 1 to 5 describe the theory of trust, Chapter 6 describes the history of trust in various countries, Chapter 7 and 8 describe the organization of trust companies, Chapter 9 describes the banking department, Chapter 10 describes the real estate department, Chapter 11 describes the custody department, Chapter 12 describes the insurance department, Chapter 13 describes the overseas Chinese department, Chapter 14 describes the travel department, Chapter 15 describes the shipping department, Chapter 16 describes valuable securities, Chapter 17 is an introduction to wills, and Chapter 18 is the accounting method of trust companies, all of which are extremely valuable. Celebrities who have inscribed titles include Hu Shuhua, Wang Zhengting, Song Ziwen, Yu Hongjun, Ma Yingbiao, Cai Zengji, Chen Guangfu, Tang Shoumin, Yang Dunfu, Ou Weiguo, Yu Hede, and Hu Zutong. Those who have written prefaces include Ma Yinchu, Li Quanshi, Zhang Wangbo, Chen Zhishuo, Lin Kanghou, and Ms. Yan Shuhe, which shows the value of the book. The pre-sale period is from July to August of this year. The book will be published on October 1. The pre-sale and sales are handled by Shanghai Trust Co. at No. 801, North Sichuan Road, this port. For details, please read the advertisement column of this newspaper.

Continental Leather Case Factory Reduces Prices

The Continental Leather Case Factory, located at the south end of the New World, was founded by the Zhou Fuzhang brothers from Ningbo. It opened last month and held a 21-day price reduction, and the business was quite developed. The various leather cases produced by the factory are all made according to Western methods, with solid materials. It is learned that the price reduction period is only seven days.

New Building Completed for Huadong Woolen Mill

Huadong Woolen Mill was founded by Chen Youyun and other Ningbo merchants in Shanghai. Its products, the Taisan Mountain trademarked plain camel wool, are of excellent quality and novel designs. Since its opening last spring, business has been exceptionally prosperous. Now, the factory's own new building at No. 174 Alabastor Road has been completed, and all offices have been moved into the new building. To facilitate customers, a general distribution office has been established at No. 60, Zunde Lane, Zhejiang Road.

News from Various Trade Unions

▲ Pharmaceutical Workers' Union: The 7th Standing Committee meeting was held yesterday, chaired by Zhao Zhenhui, to discuss various cases. (1) The Shanghai 7th District Wood and Water Industry Union was destroyed by local tyrants and hooligans, and has temporarily borrowed the 7th District Party Department for office space. A resolution was passed to issue a declaration and provide as much assistance as possible. (2) The term of office of the 5th District Executive Committee of the Union has expired, and a resolution on how to re-elect was passed to order the organization section to handle it. (3) Omitted. (4) The 3rd District Executive Committee of the Union was re-elected the day before yesterday, and 14 people, including Tong Guifang, were nominated as executives. The committee resolved to designate Tong Guifang, Xu Weiqing, Wang Meisheng, Yu Chusheng, Pan Fusheng, Lin Jinfu, and Zhao Shaowu as executive members of the 3rd District. (5) The Lianyi Cooperative society certificates affiliated with the Union were originally scheduled to be issued, but the deadline has long passed, and a few have not yet been collected. The committee resolved to send a letter to notify the members to come to the union to collect them before August 10, otherwise they will be submitted to the superior for cancellation and transferred to the Lianyi Cooperative for discussion and ratification. (6) Member Zou Bingxi came to the union the other day to exchange his membership certificate, bringing a receipt for monthly fees for October, November, and December of the 19th year. After investigation, it was found that the receipt had long been abolished, should it be valid? A resolution was passed to instruct the investigation section to investigate and handle it. (7) Should the union's old receipts and membership certificate scraps be destroyed? A resolution was passed to destroy all of them on schedule and transfer them to the council for ratification. (8) The Ye Tiande group committee sent a letter asking why the union's economic report has not been reported for a long time, and why the resolution of the general membership meeting has not been fulfilled for a long time. How should it be answered? A resolution was passed to instruct the secretary to reply to the group committee that the economic report has been sent to print and will be distributed soon. The resolution of the general membership meeting is difficult to fulfill because the time has not yet come. (9) The Shanghai 2nd District Silk Weaving Industry Union sent a letter requesting assistance from the Union due to the oppression of the capitalists. A resolution was passed to provide 10 yuan of assistance and send personnel to express condolences. (10) Since the Union changed to using stamps to collect membership fees, it has recently been heard that members often neglect to affix them. How should it be handled? A resolution was passed to first notify all members that if it is found that they have not purchased and affixed stamps for three months, they must be sanctioned in accordance with the Union regulations. If it is confirmed that they have been inadvertently omitted, they must be made up in the future. (11) It has recently been rumored that someone is falsely using the Union's name outside to swindle and deceive. How should the Union handle this? A resolution was passed to publish an advertisement in various newspapers to notify all circles that in the future, if anyone is found to be falsely using the Union's name, they should be handed over to the local military and police authorities and reported to the Union for joint submission for punishment. (12) If the directors and supervisors of the Union are insulted by the outside world for reporting improper conduct, should the Union find ways to protect them? A resolution was passed that if they are indeed insulted for official reasons, the Union will do its best to protect them.

▲ The 10th District Cotton Textile Industry Union has been approved for establishment by the Civil Training Association and issued permit No. 22. The inaugural meeting of the promoters was held yesterday, and nine people, including Tan Jiaxu, Fan Luquan, and Zhang Yilin, were elected as preparatory members. The first preparatory meeting was then held, and duties were assigned. Regarding the preparatory matters, there is a plan, and it is planned to start work immediately, and it has been submitted to various agencies.

▲ The Letterpress Printing Industry Union held its second representative meeting yesterday, with more than 80 representatives attending. Liang Yuling, Xia Jin, and Qian Shunjue were elected as the presidium. The ceremony was performed. (1) Chairman's report. (2) Reports from various representatives. (3) Passing proposals. (4) Matters for discussion. Bao Hua Printing Factory sent a letter saying that the workers were bad and handed it over to the council for handling. (5) Yixing Printing Bureau does not follow the labor-capital conditions and dismissed worker Li Songyue for no reason. The Union's mediation was refused, and a letter of warning should be sent. A unanimous resolution was passed to warn it in the name of the representative meeting. How to deal with it will be determined after convening a meeting of the branch office. (6) The dismissal of workers by Ruihua Printing Bureau was handed over to the council for handling. (7) Submit a request to the Municipal Party Department to forward it to the Central Government to request the revision of the Trade Union Law and the Factory Law, and notify the whole country to unanimously advocate anti-Japanese aid to overseas Chinese, and economic severance of relations with Japan, and insist on the conscience advocacy to the end. (8) A letter should be sent to the Anti-Japanese Association from the general meeting to ask them to order various national products stores to never increase prices by taking advantage of the opportunity. (9) Request the Municipal Party Department to forward it to the Central Government to request the rapid organization of the General Trade Union of provinces, cities, and counties. (10) The revised labor-capital contract has been delayed by the capital side's trade association, and there has been no reply. A letter should be sent immediately to notify them to come to the meeting for negotiations in three days. It was resolved to do so. (11) The representatives requested that the eight-hour work system be implemented first starting on August 1. It was resolved that it was unanimously passed. (12) Investigate whether the capitalists have joined the trade association, and then proceed with the negotiation of the contract. (13) Zhu Wenkui proposed to increase one person to be responsible for union affairs for one month. The resolution was approved. (14) Director He Yongxiang requested to resign. The resolution was approved. (15) Chen Zusheng proposed that the funds recognized by each branch office have not been paid in, or have not been fully paid in, and should be paid in immediately. The resolution was approved. (16) A small number of members have not yet collected their membership cards and badges. They should bring their money to collect them as soon as possible. It was resolved to print another notice. (17) Qian Shuntao proposed to supplement the alternate supervisors. It was resolved to elect Wang Zhiqing to serve. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 AM.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory predicted at 4:30 PM yesterday that the Yangtze River basin would be cloudy with rain, the Shandong coast would be sunny, the Korean coast would have bad weather and cyclones, the East China Sea would have southerly winds, and the Shandong wind would be undirected. Also, within 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this port was a maximum of 74.8 and a minimum of 72.0. On the same day last year, the high was 94.8 and the low was 77.7.

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor, Respectfully, after reading today's newspaper, I found that the Shanghai Women's Relief Association has quite a few criticisms of our association. Preventing problems before they arise is admirable, but the purpose of our association is purely to improve aesthetic concepts and has no malicious intent to insult women. Moreover, the holding of beauty pageants has many precedents in European and American countries. It is held every year, and tens of thousands of people flock to the streets. The grandeur is beyond words. The only goal of holding it is to enable its citizens to have a concept of beauty and to improve their physical fitness day by day. The purpose of holding this International Beauty Pageant is the same. Therefore, the women from various countries who joined have been strictly reviewed by various judges. Dastardly enchantresses hide at the sight of their shadows and have nowhere to stand. Moreover, there is no reason to force those who participate to wear bathrobes. If Chinese women join the competition, they will all wear beautiful Chinese clothes to compete for beauty. There is no distinction between high and low. Moreover, the total value of the gifts donated by major stores at sea is as high as 9,000 taels, which will be given to the elected Miss Shanghai. The preliminary and final elections will also be held in two phases. The judges are all well-known people at sea, who are impartial. The solemnity of the etiquette can be imagined. It is not comparable to a trivial matter. As for the International Bathing Beauty Contest, according to English, it was originally a mistake for the International Beauty Pageant. I am attaching this correction to avoid misunderstandings in all circles. I have always admired your newspaper's fair arguments. I hope that you will grant us the column of letters to the editor to make the truth known. I am infinitely grateful. Sincerely, The International Beauty Pageant, July 25.

Free Talk

World Short Stories

— Hai Ke

A New Weight Loss Method

Overweight people all hate their excess flesh and try every possible way to lose weight. Recently, a new weight loss method has been invented: playing the piano (Pianna) persistently. It is said to have unexpected effects. In Queensland, Australia, a person played the piano continuously for eighty-six hours and fifteen minutes, breaking all previous world records. During this time, his weight decreased by as much as thirteen pounds. If one could do this regularly, it seems it would not be difficult for a fat person to become thin. In addition, there is another method: getting very angry and flying into a rage can also reduce weight. However, family members will definitely find it a headache, and neighbors will inevitably protest.

The Haunted House in Liverpool

In Liverpool, England, there is a very beautiful house overlooking the Vale of Liangollen, with extremely beautiful scenery. Many young women from the Liverpool Women's Club Federation are now going there for summer vacation and staying there. However, this house has been known as a haunted house because, when it was built a hundred years ago, the owner, a very hygienic doctor, specially opened many holes in the walls to let air in. As a result, whenever there was a windy day, strong winds would blow in through the holes, sounding like ghosts crying. People nearby all referred to it as a haunted house. However, several years ago, all the holes were completely filled, and the sound disappeared. All so-called haunted houses in the world can be viewed in this way.

What I Saw in Nanjing

— UB

At the end of the Qing Dynasty, Nanjing had three "many's": many bedbugs, many secret prostitutes, and many candidates for official positions. After the Republic of China, there were also three "not's": dim electric lights, unreliable telephones, and uneven roads. These are all accurate criticisms.

Since Nanjing became the capital, its external appearance has greatly changed. Electric lights are bright, telephones are automatic, and roads are wide. As for the abundance of bedbugs, it is known throughout the world. The famous Nanjing bug cannot be eradicated overnight. The abundance of secret prostitutes has developed in inverse proportion to the suppression of open prostitution. This is not easy to fundamentally eliminate until the problem of people's livelihood is completely solved. However, candidates for official positions have of course disappeared. Now, it should be said that there are many officials and many belts. If we stop briefly at a playground or movie theater, we can see people wearing badges and belts everywhere.

Ryūnosuke Akutagawa wrote "The Christ of Nanjing." Western missionaries who traveled to Nanjing often wrote descriptions of Nanjing people. Foreigners' impressions of Nanjing people are almost entirely of ferocious, terrible, treacherous, and despicable characters.

Last year, a Christian missionary wrote a reflection after traveling to Nanjing. Some of his words are realistic. He said that Nanjing is a nouveau riche. Even rickshaw pullers have a barbaric and arrogant attitude. The fare is at least twenty silver cents. If you offer less, they turn their heads and ignore you, or give you a cold and mocking look.

The cost of the three necessities of life—clothing, food, and housing—has increased year by year. The cost of living in 1930 was double that of 1926, twice as expensive as in 1919-1920, and three times as expensive as in 1912-1913. Compared with the end of the Qing Dynasty, it has increased at least tenfold.

Currently, the minimum wage for a female servant in Nanjing is six yuan per month. Ten years ago, one could hire one for only one-sixth of that amount. They demand bonuses during festivals, and taking a cut of the money for buying groceries is a matter of course.

When you go to the street to buy something, you often encounter opportunities for price gouging. For example, if you use silver dimes to buy something, each dime is only counted as nine fen of a silver dollar. But if you want to give him a silver dollar and get change, he will tell you that each silver dime is worth nine fen and three li according to the market price. For example, if you buy something worth five dimes, he will give you five small silver coins and ten copper coins as change. But if you want to give him dimes, you must give him five small silver coins and fifteen copper coins. Such contradictions exist. The commercial morality of Nanjing people can be seen from this.

Mr. Wang Zhengting's Hobbies

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting celebrated his fiftieth birthday yesterday. His friends and colleagues planned to raise money to celebrate his birthday, but Mr. Wang politely declined. He then went to Hangzhou with his wife and son, and then to Mogan Mountain to avoid the birthday celebrations. At a time of natural disasters, man-made disasters, internal troubles, and external threats, Mr. Wang can understand the difficulties of the times and eliminate bad customs. He can be called a wise and outstanding person. According to a certain gentleman, several things he likes to do in his life are recorded here to confirm this talk.

Mr. Wang is good at drinking, especially Shaoxing wine. Cigars are also never far from his mouth. He is a very eloquent speaker. After a few drinks, his arguments flow endlessly, combining seriousness and humor, like wind rising and clouds forming. Those who listen are convinced. He is skilled in equestrianism. In the past, he would gallop in the countryside as his morning exercise. Recently, due to busy official duties, he has not done this for a long time. However, during his spare time, he often plays tennis, billiards, and golf with his friends. Although Mr. Wang holds important positions and is constrained by public and private affairs, he has no spare time. But his physique is strong and his spirit is full, which is largely due to outdoor exercise.

The Alarming Japanese Quest for Commercial Information in Shanghai

— Shu

The intensity of the Japanese people's desire for knowledge is as fervent as a young man pursuing the opposite sex. They seek knowledge of the Northeast, both large and small, with diligent pursuit and thorough research. Naturally, this harbors a single-minded love of treating the Northeast as their "meat on the chopping board". Look! Korea, a colony under Japanese protection, suddenly and violently rejects Chinese. This is the starting point for the Japanese's planned and orderly, single-minded love of plotting against China. If the Chinese people continue to engage in internal strife and fail to resist foreign aggression, then won't the Japanese people's long-cherished dream of the Northeast become a reality of this saying: "Where there's a will, there's a way"? The Japanese not only have the desire to swallow the Northeast, but also the evil intention of encompassing the Yangtze River. Further, they will not stop until they sweep through all of China. One can understand their conspiracy by observing the actions of the Japanese in Shanghai. Originally, the Japanese commercial organizations in Shanghai employed several Chinese people to investigate various Chinese shops: how much capital, how many shareholders, what their names are, how much revenue each year, and whether there are profits or losses; which goods are popular with which gangs, and which port sells the most of which goods. These Chinese employees have been running around all day long for more than ten years (the years of work that I know). Until now, they are still working hard without stopping. All these reports, after being sorted by the Japanese, are classified and made into tables, serving as military maps for their commercial warfare, directly delivering production to dumping sites. In this way, Chinese merchants who sell goods, due to the convenience of procedures and lower costs, naturally become the front-line shock troops of the Japanese commercial warfare. Isn't the Japanese commercial victory "as sure as having the deed in hand"? After the victory, they will probably perform the same play they put on in Korea, "driving the incense burners out of the monks," once again in mainland China. Someone said to me, "You are too worried, because this is commercialization and has nothing to do with the Japanese military." I said, "Humph. Don't be confused. They are of one mind and one heart, with the top calling and the bottom responding, standing on the same battle line to plot against us. Unlike us, who are scattered, superficial, and adhere to the ancient motto of 'each sweeping the snow from their own doorstep,' a nation without awareness or progress."

Chain of Happiness

— Xiao Die

Recently, I have repeatedly received letters from friends with a "chain of happiness," which says, "This chain can bring the best blessings and luck to people. Forward it to each other and do not interrupt it, otherwise bad luck will come immediately. This chain was invented by a US Army colonel. His intention is to make this chain circle the earth three times, and it will be miraculously effective. Copy this chain into nine copies and send them to nine good friends whom you want to bring luck to. Within nine days of sending it out, the sender will surely have very pleasant and satisfying things happen. It has been tested repeatedly and is effective, otherwise bad luck will come immediately." (Below, it lists many examples of people who gained wealth by sending the chain and lost wealth by stopping it.) This letter is often seen in the homes of relatives and friends, and it has spread all over the country. The greatness of its spread can be imagined. I dare not hope for undeserved good luck, so I have not forwarded it, and bad luck has not yet come. I only think deeply about what the inventor of this chain intends. Although it is a childish game, the speed and greatness of its spread is so rapid that if it were used for disaster relief and charity, millions of dollars could be raised in an instant. The method of nine-person chaining is to transform one into ten, ten into a hundred, a hundred into a thousand, and a thousand into ten thousand. If this chain is expanded only ten times, the number will reach one hundred million. If each person who sends a letter asks the recipient to donate one wen to a designated place and copy this letter to send to nine people, and then repeat this process, then one hundred million wen can be obtained within one hundred days, equivalent to thirty million silver dollars. When floods, droughts, and bandit disasters are rampant throughout the country, and disaster relief is lacking, why don't those who have a heart abandon useless games and pay attention to this? As long as there are ten like-minded people, making an appeal from a high place, great results can be achieved within a month.

The Strange Old Man Who Sleeps in a Coffin

— Master of Qifeng Tower

There is an old man in a certain village in Jiangyin who is from a well-off family, but he is eccentric by nature. He placed a coffin in front of his bedroom. At dusk, he would curl up and sleep in it, using it as a bed, while the bed and curtains in the room were left unused. One night, a guest, Mr. Jia, lost his way and came to his door seeking shelter. The family did not dare to respond, but Mr. Jia pleaded urgently because it was late at night and he had nowhere to stay. So they felt pity and told him, "There is indeed a spare bed in the back room, but there is a coffin in front of the bed, and strange things often happen at night. If you are brave, you can sleep there." Mr. Jia had no choice but to enter the room, read the Book of Changes by the lamp, and then lie down to sleep behind the curtain. At midnight, there was a rustling sound from the coffin. Mr. Jia held his breath and watched the strange thing from behind the curtain. After a while, an old man with a long beard lifted the coffin lid and walked to the bed, flipping through the Book of Changes and reading it. After reading it, he returned to his original place. Mr. Jia was even more horrified, but he dared not make a sound. At dawn, Mr. Jia got up to leave. Suddenly, someone came up behind him and said, "Why don't you eat your fill before you leave?" Mr. Jia looked back and was shocked and wanted to run away, because it was the person who had appeared in the coffin the night before. Then the old man explained the reason in detail, saying that the coffin lid was covered with black gauze, so it was convenient to open and use. They both smiled. This humble person says, "Now there are many thieves. Those who have wealth and cannot sleep peacefully at night may as well imitate the old man's trick to ensure safety." Just a laugh.

Travels in India (69)

— Ling Hua

On the second day, I went to Sarnath (i.e., Deer Park) again to climb a pagoda. There are three pagodas here. One is in the north, a conical brick pagoda, which cannot be climbed. The second is a pointed pagoda in the west, which is also difficult to climb. The third is a two-story pagoda in the southwest, not far from the Museum of Antiquities. Only this pagoda can be climbed. The pagoda is next to the main road, shaded by beautiful trees. There are houses nearby. I placed my bicycle next to the well and went west to climb this pagoda. There is a sign next to it, which says in English, "Chankhandhi Stuptu," which is the name of the pagoda. These signs are all made by the Mahayana Buddhist Society. There is a cave under the pagoda, which can also be entered, but I did not have time to enter due to the accumulation of broken bricks. Climbing to the second floor, I reached the top, which is about four or five zhang high. But in the open wilderness, you can see everything. You can only see the sky and clouds connected, and the dense forests of trees, interspersed with houses and wheat fields. Looking south to Varanasi, you can see chimneys. The east, west, and north are all open wilderness. Originally, Hindu temples rarely have large pagodas like those in China. There are also very few pagodas. Chinese pagodas are better than Indian pagodas. This pagoda is the birthplace of the Dharma of the Buddha's Great Enlightenment. So I wrote four lines of poetry on the north gate of the pagoda. Because I did not have a writing brush, I wrote it with a fountain pen, so the words are only barely recognizable. If a Chinese person comes, they can recognize it. The poem says, "The Dharma of the Great Enlightenment originated from the five bhikkhus. The Buddha's traces in Deer Park remain to this day. The beautiful birds and trees should be as they were yesterday. Clouds rise underfoot in the five continents."

The straight line of the top of the pagoda can be four steps. If Chinese people come to study here in the future, they can build another floor to expand it, which would be a good place to rest. I heard that the five bhikkhus lived here in the past. It has been more than two thousand years, so it can be called an ancient dormitory. I talked to the Dharma master at the university, who said that the pointed pagoda in the middle is where the Buddha first preached the Dharma. Also, many temple sites were built by King Ashoka and later kings. They have been destroyed for two thousand years, and no one cares about them. However, the bricks are still mostly intact. How solid are the projects of the ancients! I asked if there are still monks in India. He replied that there are monks in the country of Chilagon in the province of Bengal near Calcutta. Because the Buddha was originally from Kapilavastu, which belongs to this country. According to students, there are still one million people in that country today, and there may be one hundred Buddhist monks. The train can go there, and it is only two hundred miles from Calcutta. I asked how the Mahayana and Hinayana schools are divided. According to him, there was a general assembly after the Buddha's death. Two hundred years later, during the reign of King Ashoka, there was another general assembly. At that time, the Sthavira school led a group of disciples to assemble, and they became the Hinayana school. The younger ones combined and became the Mahayana school. Originally, the original name of the Hinayana school meant the school of elders, which can be proven. As for the differences in their doctrines, the Sthavira school adheres to pure cultivation and does not mix it with expedient methods. If the Mahayana school develops into multiple gods and harmonizes with Hinduism, it is an expedient method. Such are the differences between the two schools. I then returned to the Indian school. The setting sun was setting, and the cattle and sheep were returning home. The fallen leaves were falling, as if telling me that all Dharma sounds are impermanent. On the way, I passed a Christian church and met several English ladies and an Indian female missionary. They told me several passages from the Bible that can prove that women manage the world and can eliminate soldiers. Then I returned.

Rotary Club of Storytelling

??? (33)

— Xu Zhuodai

The ancients said: "A moment of spring night is worth a thousand pieces of gold, isn't a summer night worth half a cent?"

Ziliang did not speak, and lay down on the bed. His wife also followed and went up. Ziliang made way to the inside of the bed. Suddenly, he felt something high under his body. He reached out to touch it and his hand was all wet. Not good! What is it? He took it out and saw that it was a big piece of cream cake, half stuck to Ziliang's short shirt, and half still on the mattress.

This was what his wife had left by her pillow to eat, and somehow it got underneath. At that moment, when his wife saw it, she clapped her hands and laughed. Ziliang had to take off his short shirt and use it to wipe the mattress. His wife did not come to help him.

It was wiped clean! Ziliang then lay down again. When his wife saw that Ziliang did not say a word, she nagged and talked endlessly. Ziliang did not listen to her, and thought to himself:

"I originally wanted to use today's holiday to finish correcting the students' essays, more than one hundred and sixty books. But I was bothered by her, and I didn't get any work done. My mind was confused, and my body was tired. How could I write? Alas, I don't have another Sunday like this before the summer vacation. This beautiful demon, she really doesn't understand that I have important work to do. She is bothering me as a kind of duty, as a kind of fun. Alas!

Why does a man need a wife?

Is other people's wife like this?

Is this what is called the happiness of a family?" (The End)

Commercial News

Gold and Financial Markets Continue to Show Promising Trends

▲ Gold Prices Rose Six Taels Midday: Yesterday, the 25th, the posted gold price continued to rise and remained strong. There was a slight back and forth, but the situation was still stable. The trading margin was only two or three taels. As a result, it rose six taels. Transaction activity was higher than supply. The morning market immediately showed an advantage, which was not unusual given the slight increase in silver prices. It was inquired that the European market was normal and U.S. stocks fell. Because the German debt conference was not very optimistic, people were bullish, so the market opened high. It then weakened slightly, fluctuating around 744 taels. However, foreign exchange seemed good. The same industry purchased. Afterwards, it was suddenly heard that Mumbai was selling silver blocks. It rushed forward and large households competed to purchase. It quickly reached 50 taels. However, this price was not easy to sell. As the number of sellers increased, it weakened slightly. The market was closing for the week on Saturday. Remembering that this week, the market had almost become a spiral, with a high of 55 taels 2 mace, but no possibility of continuing to rise. It saw a low of 32 taels. In total, it only rose 2 taels 5 mace, etc.

▲ Early Morning Opened High: Yesterday morning, the September opening was up one tael, to 744 taels 5 mace. Large bars increased by 1/16, and the silver price also rose by 1/8. However, private telegraphs did not move. It then increased to 6 taels 5 mace. Suddenly, Yuancheng and Wupin came to sell, and it fell back to 3 taels 2 or 3 mace. It then became peaceful. There was a slight fluctuation of 1 tael. Foreign exchange did not open. The English gold price remained unchanged, and the Dongyang small reduction was 0.25, at 3 taels 2 mace, with a slight rebound of 6 or 7 mace, reaching 43 taels. Dalian Gang and Dadecheng, etc., bought in, and it rose more than 2 taels, and was favorable. Shanghai sold English gold to Zhejiang in September for 1875, reaching 5 taels 7 or 8 mace at 10 o'clock. Afterwards, because U.S. and Japanese commercial banks paired to do current period 1875, and the foreign telegraph sold U.S. dollars at 30 yuan 0.075, the gold price fell back 2 taels. Qian Changxiang, Yuan Maoyong, etc., all sold off, reaching around 44 taels at 10:20. Afterwards, English gold could be settled at 1875, and U.S. dollars were slightly favorable. On the trading floor, buyers seemed strong, and it rose to between 45 taels.

▲ Once Reached 50 Taels: Suddenly, the news that Mumbai was selling silver greatly boosted confidence. Bingxing, Daxingyong, Yu Da, Hengxingyuan, Runchangxiang, speculator Lu, etc., purchased in confusion. For a while, the atmosphere was good. It continued to rise by 4 or 5 mace, and the English gold was only settled at 1.25, reaching 50 taels at 11:00. Wanxing, Yuan Maoyong, Shunli, Hengyu, Yuancheng, etc., came to sell, so it was difficult to maintain and immediately decreased sharply by more than 2 taels, to 47 taels 8 mace. In an instant, it pulled up more than 2 taels, to 9 taels 8 mace. Xinhang, etc., bought in. Ten minutes later, it fell by more than 1 tael 5 or 6 mace, to 8 taels 2 or 3 mace. It was heard that the Indian exchange rate was small by 2 annas, and it rose by about 2 taels. By the time the market closed at noon, it was 49 taels 5 mace, an increase of 6 taels compared to the day before. Because Hengyu, Fuchang, etc., sold off, it rose back to 46 or 47 taels after closing, but there was no important news. This is just the fluctuation of confidence. The maximum midday was 50 taels and the minimum was 43 taels, a difference of 7 taels.

▲ Uncoined Silver Increased by 10 Taels: Wupin opened at 4 taels 8 mace and closed at 9 taels. The listed price was changed to 792 taels 6 mace, an increase of 50 taels.

It reached 43 or 44 taels, registered at 48 to 50 taels, supplemented water at 48 taels. The spot price for uncoined silver was slightly soft, and it increased by 10 taels. There were few transactions, and Yingfengheng, etc., had slight ins and outs.

Although the fluctuations were minor yesterday, the market continued its gradual downward trend, resulting in a slight decrease of one or two jiao to about half a yuan compared to the previous day. The total futures trading volume was over 14.48 million yuan, while there were no spot transactions in either the morning or afternoon sessions.

Yarn and Cotton: Yarn Market Temporarily Returns to Calm

The yarn market is calm, with concerns about a downward trend. This is due to the consistently declining conditions of overseas cotton yarn, yet the delivery of goods remains tight. In addition, local yarn prices are relatively high, making it difficult for prices to fall significantly at the opening. Balancing these factors, many anticipate that the domestic floods will weaken farmers' purchasing power, significantly impacting actual sales. Therefore, there are still quite a few sellers.

▲Loose Atmosphere in the Open Market: The open market at the exchange started with a flat trend. Due to the significant drop in foreign cotton, the market atmosphere was loose, with prices for all months falling by one, two, or three qian. The afternoon session remained flat, with a slight decrease of one qian for all months. The total trading volume was 28,850 bales. Purchases included 1,250 bales by Taixing, 600 bales by Hengde, 700 bales by Yichang, and 950 bales by Tongyu. Sales included 650 bales by Dafu, 2,300 bales by Guangfeng, 1,100 bales by Changfeng, 1,150 bales by Yuda, and 800 bales by Jifeng. The closing prices for the open market are recorded below:

Cotton Market: No Major Fluctuations

The decline in American cotton prices has intensified, and Indian cotton is following suit, inevitably weakening market sentiment. However, the continuous rain has caused widespread domestic flooding, significantly damaging cotton fields. Consequently, inland brokers are sending telegrams to purchase cotton. Meanwhile, local fire-powered mills are selling off large quantities due to the relatively high prices, putting pressure on the market. The afternoon session saw a decline as a result.

▲Hankou Cotton Market: Fire-Powered Mills Selling Off: The open market for Hankou cotton at the exchange initially had the potential for a sharp increase. However, due to the poor performance of foreign cotton, market sentiment softened, with prices for all months rising by one or two qian. The closing price retreated by one qian. The afternoon session declined due to fire-powered mills selling off. The closing price slightly increased as the rain continued. Overall, the price decreased by five fen. The total trading volume was 98,600 dan. Sales included 5,600 dan by Xinheng, 2,800 dan by Deji, 2,000 dan by Lichang, 2,000 dan by Yu Chang, 2,600 dan by Changfeng, and 1,800 dan by Tianlong. Grains: No Unloading of River Cargoes Due to Rain

▲Rice Price Has Increased by About Two Yuan in the Past Four Days

▲Xin Zha: Yesterday, river cargo ships could not unload due to the rain. Only Wanshengtai and Yu Changxiang were conducting business, with thick粳 and thin稻 prices increasing by three or four jiao. Compared to the rice price four days ago, the price has gradually increased by about two yuan. Yesterday, Zhenzhen opened at 15 yuan and 8 jiao for its special grade thick 粳, Wang Kun opened at 15 yuan and 2 jiao for its high-grade 粳, and Zhuyougen opened at 14 yuan and 4 jiao for its thin 稻, with only three containers available. Unloading will take place tomorrow. The source from the western route includes four or five locations such as Kunshan, Jiaoli, Jiangyin, and Wangting.

▲Nanshi: The number of people attending the market at Fengji Wharf yesterday morning was sparse. Due to the continuous heavy rain, there were no transactions on the platforms, so there was no market report. There was a lack of ships arriving from the western route, causing public anxiety. Continuous heavy rain has damaged seedlings in the inland areas, and the situation continues to show rapid increases.

Wheat Market Continues to Surge

Yesterday, the wheat market continued to surge, mainly because the rain had not stopped and the disaster was intensifying. Mature and immature rice fields have been severely affected, causing inland customers to aggressively purchase without price limits. Although another ship of foreign wheat was ordered from Australia, totaling about 7,000 tons at a price of only 4 taels, 1 qian, and 7 fen, people were actively trying to sell it off. However, buyers did not consider the foreign situation, focusing instead on the current floods, so the market could not be suppressed and continued to rise. This situation is rare recently. As a result, this month's price increased by 3 fen compared to the previous day, August increased by 4 fen, September increased by 6 fen, October increased by 5 fen, November increased by 6 fen, and December increased by 5 fen. Spot wheat and high-end mills are not moving smoothly and remain stable. 1,900 bales of wheat from Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Waigang, Penglai, Huangdu, and Jiading were opened and processed by mills such as Huafeng, Fuxin, and Xinda.

Flour Market Increases Even More Sharply

▲Inland Brokers' Buying Interest Increases Daily

Yesterday, the flour market showed another sign of increasing prices. Due to the continuous heavy rain day and night, the disasters in various places were intensifying. Therefore, inland brokers' buying interest was unwavering and continued to increase. Although the quoted price of foreign wheat was still 2 to 4 jiao lower, large and small factories also took the opportunity to sell off. However, the surging market sentiment could not be alleviated quickly, and the enthusiasm of buyers could not be diminished. The trading volume reached over 1.4 million in half a day, indicating fierce competition between both sides. This situation will lead to an increasing source of foreign wheat. As a result, this month's price increased by 1 fen and 7.5 li compared to the previous day, September increased by 2 fen and 2.5 li, October increased by 2 fen, November increased by 1 fen and 7.5 li, and December increased by 2 fen and 2 li.

Silk and Tea: Double Cocoon Goods Scarce and Prices High

▲Ordinary Opening at Eighty-Five Taels ▲Prices Increased by Two or Three Taels

This year, the cocoon production in various parts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces is unusually poor. The production of double cocoons has also decreased, and Japanese merchants are aggressively purchasing at high prices in Shanghai, further depleting inventories. Supply cannot meet demand, and prices are increasingly favorable. Yesterday, a double cocoon silk factory purchased 248 dan of ordinary double cocoons from Wuxi at a price of 85 taels, an increase of 2 or 3 taels compared to before.

Sales of Yellow and White Factory Silk to Europe Stagnant

Yesterday, the silk market at foreign firms in this area was even more deserted. The European and American markets for yellow and white factory silk were practically stagnant. Telegrams received did not indicate any improvement, and the market atmosphere was depressed. Yesterday, only Ewo and others purchased 15 packages of white dried silk, and Yongxing purchased 10 packages of yellow reeled silk. Prices remained firm.

Needle-Shaped Green Tea Sales to France Smooth

Yesterday, at foreign firms in this area, Ewo, Jardine Matheson, Tientsin & Shanghai, and Tung Foo and other firms were actively purchasing needle-shaped green tea from various regions such as Luzhuang and Tuzhuang. Transactions were not quiet, and selling prices were quite firm. Yongxing Baochang and other firms also showed some interest in high-grade Zhenmei green tea, and the market situation remained unchanged. Gongxi in Low Zhuang, Ruy Cheong Foreign Firm in Baitouzhuang also resumed business yesterday. The entire city traded over 500 boxes, with prices opening at 31 taels, about 1 or 2 taels lower than before. However, there were no transactions for goods from the upper and middle Zhuang.

Dried and Preserved Goods: New Orchid Seed Price Remarkably High

The arrival of Xiamen tangerine peel has been very scarce recently, and inventories are extremely low, causing prices to rise frequently. It was reported that 37 pieces arrived the day before yesterday and had already been opened yesterday. Good quality goods were priced at around 20 taels, while the next grade was priced at 21 taels and a half, an increase of one tael compared to before. Orchid seeds have been out of stock for a long time, and now is the time for new products to appear. Only two boxes arrived the day before yesterday, making them quite rare. The opening price reached 55 taels, the highest price ever. Many expect the market to ease after more arrivals.

Spot and futures prices for Javanese sugar also showed no fluctuations. Metals: Nanjing Arsenal Ordered Copper Yesterday via Telegraph

Yesterday, the heavy rain made the metal market even more desolate. Apart from some decorative items, there were still few bulk transactions in the entire city. However, imports of eastern metal hardware have been vigorous in recent days. Because various businesses are unable to promote sales in the inland areas, they are all preparing to register.

Shanghai Market

Market News

▲ Yongci Western Drug Store at 131 Jiangxi Road proclaims that the general manager's anti-dampness powder effectively treats dampness, rotten feet, and various skin conditions. It immediately stops pain, nourishes, prevents ulceration, promotes wound closure and muscle regeneration, and its effectiveness is quite miraculous. It is sold in major drug stores in this city.

▲ Penglai Coffee Shop inside the Penglai Market at Xiaoximen proclaims that the shop hires famous Cantonese chefs to meticulously prepare Western and American dishes. The ice cream sold is made entirely from fresh milk, fruit juice, and egg yolks, comparable to imported goods. Other cold drinks are also extremely hygienic. The elegant decorations, comfortable seating, and attentive female staff are especially praised by all sectors.

Medical News

▲ National Physician Yang Zhiyi proclaims that the doctor's original clinic was located in Huile Lane, Yunnan Road. Due to insufficient space at the old location, it has been relocated to 89 Pingle Lane, Intersection of Xizang Road and Ermalu. Consultation hours remain the same.

Page 22

Page 23

Social News Manuscript Guidelines

(1) Articles should concern domestic and international science, industry, commerce, and agriculture.

(2) News concerning hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life is limited to various aspects of social life.

(3) Photographs of seasonal scenes, landscapes, flora and fauna, people, and news-related photography are acceptable. Photographs of fashionable women in seasonal scenery are especially welcome.

(4) Each article should not exceed two thousand characters.

(5) Manuscripts should be written horizontally and legibly. Western text should be avoided where possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be appended below the translation.

Manuscripts, whether published or not, will generally not be returned. If a return is required,

(6) Do not write horizontally, and do not use sloppy characters. Western text should be avoided where possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be appended below the translation.

(7) Drawings should not be done with salt ink or colored paper, but with black ink on white paper.

(8) Please address manuscripts to the Youth Garden Editorial Department.

(9) Manuscripts, whether published or not, will generally not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three categories: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand characters. The same applies to each drawing or photograph. Special manuscripts will be remunerated separately.
